<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">1999–2000 UEFA Cup</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p>The <b>1999–2000 UEFA Cup</b> season was the 29th edition of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> competition. The final took place at <a href="/wiki/Parken_Stadium" title="Parken Stadium">Parken Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> and was won by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football_team)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football team)">Galatasaray</a>, who defeated <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in the final. The game was scoreless through the first ninety minutes and stayed that way through thirty minutes of extra time. The match went on to penalty kicks in which <a href="/wiki/Gheorghe_Popescu" title="Gheorghe Popescu">Gheorghe Popescu</a> scored the winning goal to win the cup. <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a> won the cup without losing a single game. The competition was marred by violence involving English and Turkish hooligans in the <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Cup_semi-final_violence" title="2000 UEFA Cup semi-final violence">semi-finals</a> and <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Cup_Final_riots" title="2000 UEFA Cup Final riots">the final</a>, in particular the fatal stabbings of Leeds United fans Kevin Speight and Christopher Loftus by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football_team)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football team)">Galatasaray</a> fans in Istanbul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parma_F.C." title="Parma F.C.">Parma</a> were the defending champions, but were eliminated by <a href="/wiki/SV_Werder_Bremen" title="SV Werder Bremen">Werder Bremen</a> in the fourth round.</p>
<p>It was the first season of the new format UEFA Cup; it had absorbed the now defunct <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">Cup Winners' Cup</a> to include domestic cup winners, and now featured an additional knockout round. This season's champions qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2001_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2001 FIFA Club World Championship">2001 FIFA Club World Championship</a>, which was never disputed. So far, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football_team)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football team)">Galatasaray</a> are the only <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> champions to qualify for a Club World Cup.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Association_team_allocation">Association team allocation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999%E2%80%932000_UEFA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Association team allocation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A total of 142 teams from 49 <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> associations participated in the 1999–2000 UEFA Cup. Associations are allocated places according to their 1999-2000 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_coefficient#League_coefficient" title="UEFA coefficient">UEFA league coefficient</a>.</p>
<p>Below is the qualification scheme for the 2000–01 UEFA Cup:</p>
<ul>
<li>Associations 1–6 each enter three teams</li>
<li>Associations 7–8 each enter two teams</li>
<li>Associations 9–10 each enter four teams</li>
<li>Associations 11 enters one team</li>
<li>Associations 12–15, 17, 19, 23 and 25 each enter three teams</li>
<li>Associations 16, 18, 20-22, 24 and 26-50 each enter two teams, with the exception of Liechtenstein and Andorra who enter one team each</li>
<li>3 winners of the <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Intertoto_Cup" title="2000 UEFA Intertoto Cup">Intertoto Cup</a></li>
<li>16 teams eliminated from the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_UEFA_Champions_League_qualifying_rounds#Third_qualifying_round" title="1999–2000 UEFA Champions League qualifying rounds">1999–2000 UEFA Champions League third qualifying round</a> are transferred to the UEFA Cup</li>
<li>8 teams eliminated from the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_UEFA_Champions_League#First_group_stage" title="1999–2000 UEFA Champions League">1999–2000 UEFA Champions League first group stage</a> are transferred to the UEFA Cup</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Redistribution_rules">Redistribution rules</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999%E2%80%932000_UEFA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Redistribution rules">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A UEFA Cup place is vacated when a team qualify for both the Champions League and the UEFA Cup, or qualify for the UEFA Cup by more than one method. When a place is vacated, it is redistributed within the national association by the following rules:&lt;</p>
<ul>
<li>When the domestic cup winners (considered as the "highest-placed" qualifier within the national association) also qualify for the Champions League, their UEFA Cup place is vacated, and the remaining UEFA Cup qualifiers are moved up one place, with the final place (with the earliest starting round) taken by the domestic cup runners-up, provided they do not already qualify for the Champions League or the UEFA Cup. Otherwise, this place is taken by the highest-placed league finisher which do not qualify for the UEFA Cup yet.</li>
<li>When the domestic cup winners also qualify for the UEFA Cup through league position, their place through the league position is vacated, and the UEFA Cup qualifiers which finish lower in the league are moved up one place, with the final place taken by the highest-placed league finisher which do not qualify for the UEFA Cup yet.</li>
<li>A place vacated by the League Cup winners is taken by the highest-placed league finisher which do not qualify for the UEFA Cup yet.</li>
<li>A Fair Play place is taken by the highest-ranked team in the domestic Fair Play table which do not qualify for the Champions League or UEFA Cup yet.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teams">Teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=1999%E2%80%932000_UEFA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The labels in the parentheses show how each team qualified for the place of its starting round:</p>
<ul>
<li>CW: Cup winners</li>
<li>CR: Cup runners-up</li>
<li>LC: League Cup winners</li>
<li>Nth: League position</li>
<li>P-W: End-of-season European competition play-off winners</li>
<li>FP: Fair play</li>
<li>IT: Intertoto Cup winners</li>
<li>UCL: Relegated from the Champions League
<ul>
<li>GS: Third-placed teams from the group stage</li>
<li>Q3: Losers from the third qualifying round</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
